Salmon Farming Industry Handbook 2024 
Salmon Farming 
Industry Handbook
2024 
Mowi is one of the world’s leading 
seafood companies, ranked number 
one on both market capitalisation and 
sustainability. Mowi is also by far the 
world’s largest Atlantic salmon farmer 
with harvest volumes of 501 530 tonnes 
in 2024, equivalent to a global market 
share of approximately 20%. The 
company has a fully integrated value 
chain from roe to plate and produces 
its own environmentally certified feed 
specifically designed for the Mowi 
salmon strain.
This integrated report sets out how 
we run our business and describes our 
vision, our ambition, our successes and 
our improvement areas in an open 
and transparent way. 
At every stage of the value chain, we 
all work towards one shared aim: To 
provide a growing world population 
with delicious, healthy and nutritious 
food from the ocean, in a way that 
respects our planet and allows local 
communities to flourish. A product 
everyone at Mowi is proud of, every 
day.

From backyard beginnings to world leadership
Since the Mowi adventure started in 1964, we have continued to 
invest in our value chain and today enjoy full control of our product, 
from the parental broodstock to sales. It’s a remarkable story. From 
its humble beginnings, when a few pioneers started farming fish in 
their backyards, Mowi has become a global leader in its field. 
60 years later, our investments in areas such as genetics, smolt, 
value-added processing and smart technology have transformed 
our business and now place us in a leading position that few foodproducing companies can match.

Mowi is the world's largest producer of farm-raised 
salmon measured by both volume and turnover. We 
offer seafood products to more than 70 countries, 
are represented in 26 countries and employ 11 700 
people. Mowi is organised in three business areas: 
Feed, Farming and Sales & Marketing.
Sales & Marketing
Includes our secondary processing and value-added operations in Europe, 
the US and Asia, and the sales and delivery of our products. 
Feed
Comprises our feed plants in Norway and Scotland.
(Tonnes) Production
 
 
Farming
Incorporates our farming operations and some primary processing and filleting 
activities in Norway, Scotland, Canada, Chile, Ireland, the Faroe Islands and 
Iceland.

012 LEADING THE BLUE REVOLUTION STRATEGY BOARD STATEMENTS FINANCIAL STATEMENTS ANALYTICAL APPENDICES 013
Unlocking the potential of the sea
"The world needs more food from the ocean. Blue foods have 
a key role in providing healthy and climate-friendly food for 
a growing world population. By providing more than 8 million 
healthy and sustainable meals every day, Mowi is part of the 
solution to provide food, nutrition and employment."

The world needs more food 
from the ocean
was close to 40 million postsmolt, equivalent to a quarter of Mowi's 
annual smolt production. The postsmolt share in Mowi Norway was 
50% when excluding the naturally more resilient Region North, and 
approx. 30% in Mowi Scotland. 
Mowi also continues to pursue accretive M&A opportunities. At the 
beginning of 2025, Mowi entered into a share purchase agreement 
to increase its ownership in Nova Sea from 49% to 95%. Nova Sea 
is a leading fully integrated salmon farmer in production area 8 in 
Northern Norway and covers the value chain from broodstock and 
smolt production to harvesting and sales. The company expects 
to harvest 52k GWT of salmon in 2025. Mowi has been a large 
minority owner in Nova Sea since 1995 and knows the company 
well. Nova Sea is a pioneer of the Norwegian aquaculture industry 
and is known for its excellent biological performance and industryleading margins. Over 50 years, the company and the Olaisen 
family have invested in the organisation and developed it into an 
impressive operation. It is therefore with great pleasure that we are 
now, after 30 years, combining our operations (subject to customary 
closing conditions, including approval from competition authorities).
Mowi's 2029 volume target announced at the Capital Markets Day 
in September 2024 has been increased from 600k GWT to exceed 
650k GWT with Nova Sea on board. For the group, this translates 
into annual growth of 6.1% since 2018, or as much as 225k GWT. 
To put this figure into perspective, it is about the annual volumes 
harvested by the world's second largest salmon farmer. Mowi has 
indicated an investment need of approx. EUR 600 million to reach 
this volume target. The group now expects to reach 600k GWT 
already in 2026, with Mowi Norway alone expecting to exceed 400k 
GWT in 2029.
2024 was a record year for Mowi and the company 
achieved several milestones. Operational revenue 
of EUR 5.62 billion was the highest ever, driven by 
record-high volumes of 502k tonnes. In the Farming 
segment, seawater production was the best 
ever, and stocking of postsmolt to sea reached 
a new high. Furthermore, Mowi set new volume 
and revenue records in Consumer Products and 
Feed, as well as all-time high annual earnings 
in Feed. Operational EBIT for the group was EUR 
829 million, equivalent to underlying earnings per 
share of EUR 1.05. The company has delivered 
on its three strategic pillars – volume growth, 
cost competitiveness and sustainability. These 
achievements were only made possible by the 
dedication and hard work of Mowi’s employees.
Group operational revenue was EUR 5 617 million (EUR 5 513 
million) driven by all-time high volumes, while market prices were 
slightly down. Price achievement was also affected by quality 
downgrading in Norway in the first half of the year. 
In Farming, harvest volumes for 2024 were all-time high at 502k 
GWT (475k) following strong production and increased smolt 
stocking. In our three largest Farming units, Norway, Scotland and 
Chile, volumes were record-high with new production milestones 
achieved. 
Volume growth across our business areas is a key value driver 
and one of Mowi’s strategic pillars. Growth within Mowi Farming 
has been impressive in recent years, and 2024 marked another 
good year with all-time high harvest volumes of 502k GWT, 
equivalent to growth of 5.7% vs. industry supply growth of 1.3%. 
In 2025, Mowi’s volume guidance is 530k tonnes, representing 
another year of solid growth equivalent to 5.7%. This is supported 
by record-high biomass in sea which was 10% higher year-on-year. 
As recently as 2018, harvest volumes were 375k GWT, hence we 
will have grown our farming volumes by 155k GWT in the period 
to 2025, equivalent to a CAGR of 5.1% versus a projected CAGR 
for the industry of 2.8%. This is mainly organic growth, and Mowi 
has initiated further initiatives that are still expected to contribute 
to additional organic volume growth. The most important initiative 
in this respect is postsmolt, i.e. robust and large smolt which has 
several advantages. By increasing smolt stocking and producing 
postsmolt, Mowi will further improve its license utilisation. Postsmolt 
production increases license turnover, improves biological KPIs 
through shorter production time in sea and better survival rates, 
and reduces cost. At the end of 2024, postsmolt capacity in Mowi

This impressive volume growth has been realised in the last years, 
following a more growth-focused and Farming-oriented strategy 
for Mowi which resulted in the implementation of a long list of 
measures. In the years preceding the large merger back in 2007, 
volumes were in fact quite stable until 2019 onwards.
Consumer Products, our value-added leg, delivered Operational 
EBIT of EUR 145.8 million (EUR 151.7 million) equivalent to ROCE of 
19.0%, and record-high volumes of 247k tonnes product weight. 
These are stellar results in a highly competitive business. Mowi's 
Smart Factories concept, managed by our global Mowi Processing 
Excellence Team, drives the introduction of more modern 
technologies and automation across our factories to reduce 
cost and increase value. Mowi also continues to develop new 
innovative and high-quality products that are easily accessible to 
our customers, to keep pace with constantly evolving food habits. 
Our branded MOWI products have supported these developments 
by growing consumer awareness and loyalty to our products. 
MOWI is now a trusted name in 16 countries across Europe, the US 
and Asia, and Mowi will continue its branding strategy unabated in 
2025 and the years ahead.
Mowi Feed can also celebrate its best year so far with Operational 
EBITDA of EUR 62.2 million. Sold volumes reached a new record 
high of 585k tonnes for the full year, up 12% year-on-year following 
strong growth in sea and consequently good feed demand. To 
cater for growing feed demand, Mowi Feed is expanding the 
Norwegian feed plant with a new production line adding 60k 
capacity. This brings the capacity of our two state-of-the-art feed 
mills to 460k tonnes in Norway and 240k tonnes in Scotland, 
i.e. 700k tonnes capacity in total. In March 2025, Mowi initiated 
a strategic review of the Feed division. In just a few years, Mowi 
has grown from a 400k GWT farmer to approaching a 600k GWT 
farmer with production in seven countries and 11 farming regions 
with all the complexity that entails. Mowi also has an extensive 
downstream business. In order to streamline our operations, the 
time is ripe to assess how our Feed division will be organised in 
the future. The review will assess all available options, including a 
sale.
On cost, Mowi is the best or second best performer in all the 
regions where we farm salmon. We are now also the best 
performer in Norway, based on average figures for the last three 
years. We are also ahead in our downstream operations. Cash 
cost-to-stock fell throughout 2024 driven by lower feed prices and 
consequently we expect lower P&L released-from-stock cost in 
2025. Furthermore, we expect the positive feed price development 
to continue. In 2024, the organisation delivered on its cost-cutting 
targets for the year, achieving EUR 42 million in annualised savings. 
A total of EUR 327 million in annualised savings has been achieved 
since Mowi's cost savings programmes began in 2018. Addressing 
cost has become engrained in Mowi’s workflow, and the company 
has initiated another global cost savings programme for 2025 with 
a target of EUR 30 million of savings during the year which comes 
in addition to targeted savings in the areas of postsmolt, Mowi 4.0, 
productivity and efficiency. At the Capital Markets Day in 2024, 
Mowi announced a total cost reduction potential in the range of 
EUR 300-400 million over the coming five years.
Mowi decided in 2020 to include a productivity programme in the 
cost savings programme, targeting a 10% reduction in FTEs for 
the company as-is by 2024. By year-end 2024, FTEs had been 
reduced by a total of 3 161 FTEs on a like-for-like basis, equivalent 
to a full 21%. FTEs in 2024 were 13 806, 6% fewer than 14 998 in 
2019, despite 15% higher volumes, and consequently we have 
over-delivered on the 10% like-for-like target set back in 2020. In 
2025, the target is to reduce FTEs by another 300 through the 
productivity programme.
For the sixth consecutive year, Mowi was ranked top in the Coller 
FAIRR Protein Producer Index, the comprehensive assessment of 
the largest listed animal protein producing companies on critical 
environmental, social and governance issues. Mowi's mission to 
provide sustainable and healthy food to a growing world population 
is crucial. To yet again occupy the top position in the prestigious 
Coller FAIRR ranking is extremely encouraging and demonstrates 
that Mowi is at the forefront of sustainable food production. Salmon 
has superior sustainability credentials, including carbon footprint, 
compared with other animal proteins. Mowi's salmon production

Feed
Mowi's feed performs very well, which is an essential quality as 
feed is the most important input factor in salmon production. 
Mowi is self-sufficient for feed in Europe with our state-of-theart plants in Valsneset, Norway and Kyleakin, Scotland. Sold 
volumes reached 584 586 tonnes for the year, an increase of 
12% from 2023 on good growth in sea and higher volumes, and 
consequently higher demand for feed. Operational EBITDA came 
in at EUR 62.2 million (EUR 52.1 million), equivalent to a margin of 
5.5%. Mowi Feed's core assets include a 460,000 tonnes feed 
mill in Norway and a 240,000 tonnes feed mill in Scotland, i.e. a 
combined capacity of 700,000 tonnes. These figures include an 
ongoing 60,000 tonnes capacity expansion in Norway expected 
to be fully operational in Q2 2026. In March 2025, Mowi initiated 
a strategic review of the Feed division. The background is 
Mowi's significant growth in farming volumes the last few years, 
and the complexity related to being a 600k GWT farmer with 
production in seven countries and 11 farming regions. Mowi also 
has an extensive downstream business. In order to streamline 
our operations, now is the time to assess how our Feed division 
will be organised in the future. The review will assess all available 
options, including a sale.
Farming
Mowi Farming works along three strategic pillars: Volume growth, 
cost, and sustainability. In recent years, Mowi has achieved 
strong results across all these areas. With regards to cost, 
Mowi Farming is competitive and is the best or the second-best 
cost performer vs. peers in the regions in which the company 
operates. The company has implemented a culture which is more 
focused on cost and FTEs to address the underlying inflation and 
cost pressure in the industry. On sustainability, Mowi has been 
ranked #1 amongst listed animal protein producers for the sixth 
consecutive year, and survival rate, seawater production rate and 
feed conversion ratio were all improved in 2024 vs. 2023. The 
ramp-up of postsmolt volumes and the ongoing implementation 
of Smart Farming and other Mowi 4.0 technologies are expected 
to have a positive impact not only on productivity and costs, but 
saves the world 2 million tonnes of CO2e emissions annually by 
replacing the corresponding amount of land animal protein production. 
In addition to the positive ESG credentials with regards to the product 
itself, Mowi has ambitious targets for further reducing the carbon 
footprint related to the company's activities.
Mowi is by far the largest producer of salmon, a scientifically proven 
natural superfood. Salmon is versatile and appeals to people of all 
ages with its highly appetising taste, look, texture and colour. The 
megatrends driving salmon demand are strong and driven by health 
trends and a growing need for more low-carbon diets, more food from 
the ocean and less ultra-processed food. With its size, integrated value 
chain, global market presence and focus on operational excellence, 
Mowi is well positioned to capitalise on these megatrends. Mowi, with 
a proud 60-year history going back to the very start of the salmon 
farming industry, is working on many important initiatives that will 
further develop the company and propel it into the future. In Farming, 
we are working along three main pillars; volume growth, cost and 
sustainability. In Sales & Marketing, we are putting the customer at the 
core of all our activities related to products, branding and operational 
excellence. As regards the Feed division, we continue to work on 
operational improvements and cost optimisation, and it is encouraging 
to see that our feed is performing very well.
In 2025, Mowi will continue to invest across the value chain to support 
further organic growth and strengthen the asset base. The capital 
expenditure budget for 2025 is approximately EUR 310 million, up from 
EUR 290 million in 2024, with the majority of investments allocated to 
the Farming segment. Three large postsmolt investments in Norway 
have already been completed, and in 2025 we will invest further into 
selected seawater expansion initiatives across our farming footprint, as 
well as finalising the new broodstock facility in Scotland. We are also 
investing in postsmolt in closed containment systems in sea as well as 
lice lasers and submerged pens. In addition to the expected positive 
operational and financial effects, these investments will contribute 
to our efforts to further improve fish welfare and sustainability. 
Furthermore, Consumer Products expects to undertake several 
automation and packaging technology projects, and Mowi Feed is 
investing in increased capacity. 
With effect from 2 April 2025, 25% tariffs have been imposed on 
goods imported from Canada to the USA. The situation is fluid and it 
is difficult to see how this will play out, including other countries. Mowi 
will continuously monitor any developments related to this subject and 
will be prepared to redistribute our volumes from our seven origins 
with respect to prevailing trade policies at any given time to best serve 
our customers.
We believe in a positive market outlook for the company. Supply 
growth has been limited in recent years and we do not expect 
significant volume growth for the industry in the next five years. This 
would under normal circumstances be supportive of good salmon 
prices. We expect global megatrends to continue to drive demand 
for salmon and we expect demand growth to outpace supply growth, 
despite short-term headwinds from the generally increased cost of 
living, particularly in the US. With good operational performance as 
a backdrop, the organisation is well set to deliver on its ambitious 
targets over the coming years.
also on fish welfare and sustainability. When it comes to volume 
growth, Mowi Farming has grown more than the industry, and 
based on 2025 guidance of 530,000 GWT (excluding Nova Sea), 
volume growth since 2018 equals 155,000 GWT or 5.1% CAGR vs. 
2.8% for the wider industry. In Mowi Norway, our largest and most 
important farming entity, harvest volumes reached a record-high 
level of 304k GWT in 2024 and license utilisation and production 
efficiency are industry-leading. The guidance of 315k GWT for 
Mowi Norway in 2025 implies growth of 85k GWT since 2018 and 
an impressive CAGR of 4.6% vs. 3.1% for the industry. Mowi's goal 
is to continue to capture market share in the salmon category 
in the coming years by growing its farming volumes, both 
organically and acquisitively. Mowi has initiated further organic 
growth initiatives, including postsmolt, which are expected to 
contribute to continued volume growth above the overall industry 
level.

NORWAY LICENSE UTILISATION
Industry
In 2021, Mowi Farming launched a venture into postsmolt. 
Following completion of the Fjæra (Norway Region South) 
and Nordheim (Norway Region Mid) facilities in 2023 and the 
Haukå (Norway Region West) facility in 2024, approx. 40% of the 
postsmolt programme in Mowi Norway is completed. Mowi Norway 
also has postsmolt production in semi-closed containment systems 
in sea. The results of these investments are now beginning to 
show and at year-end 2024, the postsmolt share in Mowi Norway 
was approx. 50% when the naturally more resilient Region North 
is excluded from the equation. In Mowi Scotland, the share was 
approx. 30%, and the total postsmolt capacity in Mowi was close to 
40 million postsmolt, equivalent to a quarter of the smolt produced 
annually. This is expected to further improve license utilisation 
and result in improved biological KPIs including survival rates and 
average harvest weights. 
018 LEADING THE BLUE REVOLUTION STRATEGY BOARD STATEMENTS FINANCIAL STATEMENTS ANALYTICAL APPENDICES 019
Ivan Vindheim
Chief Executive Officer
Mowi owns 51% of the shares in Icelandic salmon farmer Arctic Fish. 
Mowi's clear goal is to develop Arctic Fish into a streamlined and 
cost-effective operation. Volume guidance for 2025 is 15,000 GWT, 
and volumes are expected to increase steadily in the coming years. 
Mowi also has some inherent growth opportunities in its operations 
in Ireland and the Faroes. Combined volume guidance for 2025 
from these two regions is 20,000 GWT.
Mowi's volumes should increase beyond 650,000 GWT by 2029 
through reaping the fruits of the postsmolt investments completed 
so far and adding on the volumes from Nova Sea. The company 
would then still have organic growth opportunities within the 
current license footprint. This comes in addition to further potential 
M&A activities and purchasing of additional capacity. Mowi's clear 
strategy is to continue to grow more rapidly than the industry as a 
whole. 
Sales & Marketing
This division contains all our downstream activities, including 
our steadily growing production of consumer-ready products. 
Operational results for Consumer Products were strong with 
Operational EBIT of EUR 145.8 million. Demand was generally 
good, and Consumer Products sold a record-high 247 333 tonnes 
of finished products, proving that putting the customer at the core 
of everything we do downstream bears fruit and creates unique 
customer experiences.
Mowi will further enhance our value proposition downstream in the 
years to come, and our branding strategy, with its ultimate goal of 
de-commoditising the salmon category, will play a key part in this. 
Demand for our MOWI-branded products is increasing. We have 
great belief in our MOWI brand strategy, and our long-term target of 
EUR 1 billion in turnover at 10% earnings margin remains in place.
Within our Sales & Marketing division there is a strong focus on 
automation and digitalisation, where our cross-border Processing 
Excellence team has been tasked with realising improvements 
in our processing plants. By establishing benchmarks and best 
practices, the team will continue to focus on automation and 
the right use of technology to further improve our processing 
operations, ensuring efficient and lean factories. We are the largest 
value-added operator in the salmon sector with 33 primary and 
secondary facilities in 20 countries and our plans to realise further 
operational improvements continue unabated. 
Sustainability
Farming the ocean holds the key to ensuring a stable, healthy 
and sustainable food source for a growing world population. 
Aquatic food is a nutritional powerhouse, rich in protein, essential 
fatty acids, vitamins and vital minerals. It provides income and 
jobs, particularly in coastal regions, and supports flourishing local 
economies and communities. The benefits of farming the ocean 
extend to our planet as well. The ocean provides billions of people 
with nutritious food, with a much smaller environmental footprint 
than land-animal food production. In fact, a dietary shift from landbased animal protein to aquatic food is recognised as a vital step 
towards achieving more sustainable food systems.
In recent years, food systems and in particular aquatic or blue 
food systems have been high on the agenda with increasing 
recognition of their potential to solve global planetary challenges 
such as food insecurity and climate change. In 2024, FAO released 
its updated State of the World Fisheries and Aquaculture report 
(SOFIA), showing for the first time that aquaculture has surpassed 
capture fisheries in aquatic animal production, contributing over 
57% of aquatic animal products used for direct human consumption. 
This significant milestone underscores the growing importance 
of aquaculture in meeting global food demands, with production 
expected to increase by 10% by 2032, driven by aquaculture 
expansion. Continued high consumption of food products with 
high GHG footprints, including land animal proteins, contributes 
unnecessarily to the emissions of agrifood systems. We believe that 
aquaculture and salmon farming are well positioned to facilitate a 
much needed dietary shift and to deliver food from the ocean in a 
sustainable way. 
We remain committed to the principles of the United Nations' Global 
Compact and to maximising our contribution to its Sustainable 
Development Goals (SDG). At Mowi, we pursue an integrated 
sustainability strategy where long-term targets have been 
established for all our guiding principles: Planet, People, Product 
and Profit. For the first year Mowi is reporting on the Corporate 
Sustainability Reporting Directive (CSRD) from the EU. 
Our sustainability strategy, Leading the Blue Revolution Plan, 
reflects Mowi's commitment to sustainable development. In 2024, 
we continued the implementation of our sustainability strategy, 
and demonstrated progress in key strategic programmes and 
reduction in Mowi's scopes 1 and 2 GHG emissions in line with our 
Science Based targets (SBT). Mowi has set climate targets aligned 
with 1.5° C which also include reduction in GHG emissions from 
Forest, Land and Agriculture (FLAG). We continue to develop new 
policies and update existing ones to reflect the input we get from 
our stakeholders. It is encouraging that our work in this area has 
been recognised, including by the Coller FAIRR Protein Producer 
Index which Mowi topped for the sixth consecutive year. The index 
assesses 60 of the largest listed global meat, dairy and aquaculture 
companies on ten environmental, social and governance themes 
aligned with the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs). Overall, 
Mowi was rated ‘Industry Best’ on many of the criteria aligned to the 
SDGs including sustainability governance, water use & scarcity and 
waste & pollution. In 2024, Mowi was also named one of world's 
most sustainable companies in the world by Time Magazine. 
'Leading a Blue Revolution' is not easy but we believe Mowi’s 
unique strengths – our global presence, being fully integrated and 
being a front runner on innovation and R&D – will make a positive 
impact in the world.
Chile's efforts to further improve operations, the use of freshwater 
treatments have been ramped up, with good results so far.
With regards to Canada, the imposition of 25% tariffs on goods 
imported from Canada to the US with effect from 4 March 2025 adds 
uncertainty. The situation is fluid and it is difficult to see how this will 
play out, including other countries. Mowi monitors developments 
and is prepared to redistribute volumes from our seven origins with 
respect to prevailing trade policies at any given time to best serve 
our customers. 
In addition to tariffs, framework conditions for Mowi Canada West 
have been adversely impacted by the authorities' decision in June 
2024 to ban traditional marine salmon farming from mid-2029. 
Consequently, Mowi Canada West is a 20k GWT level operation with 
uncertain future prospects. Following the political decision, Mowi 
initiated a strategic review of the Canada West business unit and will 
explore all available options before taking appropriate action. 
The situation related to tariffs is also negative for Canada East. 
In this region, Mowi has experienced several environmental and 
biological incidents since the acquisition of Northern Harvest in 2018. 
However, in the last few years, ISA detections and sea lice levels 
have improved and the region has secured a steady improvement 
in farming performance and biological KPIs. The cost curve has also 
improved considerably. On the back of improved biological control 
and reduced cost at stock, volumes are expected to increase in the 
coming years. Volumes were 8k GWT in 2024 and are guided to 
increase to 16k GWT in 2025. Mowi still has many unused licenses 
in this region and there is significant potential for growth. The 
government decision in Canada West related to licenses does not 
affect Canada East.
In Scotland, Mowi has experienced increasingly challenging 
environmental conditions over the past few years, driven by rising 
seawater temperatures, and this has also negatively impacted 
cost. This development calls for more robust salmon and a shorter 
production cycle in sea in order to, amongst other things, avoid 
a second summer and autumn in sea. With this in mind, Mowi 
acquired the Dawnfresh bankruptcy estate's Loch Etive trout 
sites in 2023 and has converted sites from trout production to 
postsmolt salmon production. The first postsmolts were transferred 
to ordinary marine sites in 2024 and will be harvested in 2025. 
At year-end 2024, postsmolt coverage in Scotland was 30%, 
with lower capital expenditure, shorter realisation time and lower 
running production cost than an equivalent land-based solution. 
Another important part of Mowi Scotland's biological turnaround 
plan is to become self-sufficient for eggs. Mowi Scotland is 
therefore constructing a new bespoke broodstock and egg 
facility at Ardessie in Northern Scotland. When complete in 2025, 
it will provide a secure supply for 100% of Mowi Scotland's egg 
requirements. Mowi Scotland is also developing new sites to 
utilise new licenses awarded in recent years. 2025 volumes for 
Mowi Scotland are guided at 70k GWT, up from an all-time high 
66k GWT in 2024. In 2029, expected volumes are 80k GWT, and 
processing capacity is being expanded to handle this increase. 
In Mowi's operations in Chile, overall biology and cost 
performance have been good. Mowi expects to grow volumes 
from 73k GWT in 2024 to 77k GWT in 2025 and plans to increase 
volumes in the coming years in line with the traffic light system 
in Chile which aims at controlling the industry's sanitary situation. 
In 2029, expected volumes are 95k GWT. Mowi Chile continues 
to focus on efficient production and low cost, and one of the 
recent initiatives is a trial of a new SRS vaccine. As part of Mowi

Our corporate foundation 
We believe that by farming the ocean, we can sustainably produce 
healthy, nutritious and tasty food for society at large. 70% of our 
planet is covered by water, yet the United Nations Food and 
Agriculture organisation (FAO) estimates that only around 2% 
of the world’s food caloric supply comes from the ocean. This 
includes both farm-raised and wild-caught fish. We know that global 
consumption of farm-raised seafood will increase in the future, 
both in terms of overall volumes and as a percentage of the global 
food supply. The biennially FAO report (Sofia, 2024) on the state of 
world fisheries and aquaculture estimates that rising incomes and 
urbanisation, improvements in post-harvest practices and changes in 
dietary trends are projected to drive a 12% increase in aquatic food 
consumption by 2032, reaching an average of 21.3 kg per capita.
The Mowi way – From vision to action 
Our financial results are created through interaction between people, 
the natural environment and technology. Our goal is to find an 
optimal combination of these elements to create long-term success, 
whilst understanding that our growth must be environmentally, 
socially and financially sustainable. To manage the risks that may 
prevent us from reaching our goals and delivering on our strategy, 
we have developed the “Mowi Way”. The Mowi Way combines our 
vision, values, strategy, leadership, and our guiding principles.
Our vision
Our vision, “Leading the Blue Revolution”, gives direction and 
outlines possibilities. The possibilities lie in the increased need 
for protein to supply a growing and increasingly prosperous world 
population with healthy, sustainable food products. We believe the 
most efficient way to produce more protein is by farming the ocean.
Guiding principles 
The way we operate our business is centred around our four guiding 
principles that underpin our vision and behaviour: Planet, Product, 
People and Profit. Balancing the four principles is a prerequisite 
for Leading the Blue Revolution and creating long-term value. This 
ensures that we continue to deliver a premium product with minimal 
negative impact to the environment that also generates value for 
the local communities in which we operate, as well as focusing 
upon delivering healthy shareholder returns and ensuring access to 
capital.
Our strategy 
We aim to be an integrated provider of proteins from the ocean, 
taking the lead in all key areas. By integrating the value chain, we 
can control our products from roe to plate, and be more proactive in 
addressing various challenges. We see research and development 
as an integral part across our value chain, which differentiates Mowi 
within the industry. 
From Vision to Action
023
Vertical integration
We believe there are benefits to vertical integration, due to the 
greater capacity it gives us to control the production process. 
We refer to activities which occur after farming (i.e. secondary 
processing) as downstream operations, and activities occurring 
prior to farming (i.e. feed production) as upstream operations. Our 
integrated production helps us stabilise costs, control the quality of 
our products and improve efficiency. Over time, vertical integration 
is expected to result in more stable earnings and unlock future 
growth. We expect to be less exposed to the cyclical nature of 
salmon prices, and to be better able to control the quality of our 
products. An important prerequisite for building the MOWI brand 
and gaining brand awareness is to gain consumer trust, and through 
Mowi's integrated value chain, we believe that the company can 
differentiate the way our products are perceived, positioned and 
sold. 
Our leadership principles
Taking the lead is about setting a course and taking responsibility, 
and our leadership principles provide an important guide for 
managers’ behaviour:
Inspire people: We recruit the very best and build talent for the 
future. We strive to create winning teams and challenge people to 
succeed.
Make it happen: We challenge existing thinking and promote 
change and innovation. We encourage people to propose solutions 
and learn from mistakes.
Live the values: We want our leaders to be role models and 
build our culture; leaders should show direction and engage with 
stakeholders.
Think and act: We want our leaders to think and act as if the 
company was their own. Leaders should do what is best for the 
company, bearing in mind both our short- and long-term goals.
Our values 
Our global values — Passion, Change, Trust and Share — inspire us 
to act in the right way and are key enablers for reaching our goals. 
Passion for the company and the product: Passion is the key to our 
success and how we make a difference.
Change is the new “normal”: We are ready for change and work 
continuously to improve our operations.
Trust is essential in everything we do: Our operations provide safe, 
delicious and healthy food, and we deliver on our promises.
Share underpins the performance of our employees: We share 
knowledge and experience, we are open and transparent, and we 
cooperate with key stakeholders globally.

030 LEADING THE BLUE REVOLUTION STRATEGY BOARD STATEMENTS FINANCIAL STATEMENTS ANALYTICAL APPENDICES 031
Overall Group Performance in 2024
Operational revenues in 2024 amounted to EUR 5 616.6 million, an 
increase of 1.9% from 2023. This was driven by record-high harvest 
volumes of 501 530 tonnes gutted weight of salmon in 2024, up 
from 474 664 tonnes in 2023. Market prices were slightly reduced 
from a high level in 2023, and quality downgrading in Norway in the 
first half of the year had a negative effect. Operational EBIT came 
in at EUR 828.9 million in 2024, compared with EUR 1 027.5 million 
for the year ended December 31, 2023. The decrease was driven 
by lower achieved prices. While cash cost to stock decreased 
during 2024, realised P&L cost in Farming increased somewhat 
from 2023 driven by previous inflation. Our earnings before financial 
items (EBIT) totalled EUR 758.6 million in 2024, compared with EUR 
981.0 million in 2023. We achieved a return on capital employed 
(ROCE) of 15.5% in 2024, above our long-term target of 12.0%. The 
comparable figure for 2023 was 21.3%. At year-end, the Group had 
a net interest-bearing debt (NIBD) of EUR 1 867 million, above the 
long-term NIBD target of EUR 1 700 million. The NIBD target will be 
revised following closing of the Nova Sea acquisition. NIBD at yearend 2023 was EUR 1 790 million.
The Market in General 
Supply
2024 marked a year with lower global commodity prices as rising 
cost of living in an inflationary environment took its toll on consumer 
demand in many end markets. The salmon market was not insulated

Reference prices
The reference price for salmon of Norwegian origin decreased 
slightly in the market currency from a high level in 2023. This 
was also the case for Seattle prices. The average price in Miami 
increased by 3.4% for the year, and the Boston/New York reference 
price decreased by 6.1%.
from these effects, however, demand fundamentals for salmon 
fared quite well in this context all the same. The overall global value 
for salmon at farm gate prices was estimated at approx. EUR 20 
billion in 2024 which was stable versus 2023. The estimated global 
blended salmon price declined marginally by 1% on a global supply 
increase of 1%. Market expectations for 2025 are favourable with 
an expectation of higher salmon prices on recovering demand and 
modest supply growth. Global industry harvest volume of Atlantic 
salmon was approximately 2 541 500 tonnes gutted weight in 
2024. This was 25 200 tonnes more than in 2023, an increase of 
1.0%. Supply from Norway increased by 28 000 tonnes in 2024 
on generally improved biological KPIs in sea resulting in improved 
production and harvesting. Supply from Scotland increased 
by 31 200 tonnes, equivalent to 22.6% y-o-y, due to improved 
biological conditions, improved fish welfare and higher survival 
rates. Supply from Chile decreased by 59 400 tonnes on slightly 
lower growth than expected in the start of the year and some 
delayed harvesting into 2025.

Global consumption increased by 3.0% in 2024 compared with 
2023 including inventory adjustments. The estimated global value 
of salmon remained at a record-high level, demonstrating the strong 
underlying growth drivers for salmon as a nutritious and sustainable 
source of protein. 
Consumption in the EU and the UK increased by 5.6% compared 
with 2023 on increased supply and product availability. Overall, the 
European market experienced good demand developments in the 
retail segment with the fresh category leading the way. Demand 
developments within the foodservice segment, on the other hand, 
were relatively stable. In the last part of the year the foodservice 
sector saw some higher activity, indicating some rebound from the 
downturn caused by the increased cost of living. 
The US market consumed close to 600k tonnes, equivalent to a 
market share of 22%. After several years with growth in excess 
of the wider market, consumption was reduced by 3.1% in 2024. 
Availability of volumes from Chile was reduced vs. 2023. While 
the US market lags somewhat behind Europe in terms of demand 
recovery, the retail channel experienced volume growth. The fresh 
pre-packed category continued to drive retail developments. 
Consumption in the Asian market increased by 6.2% compared with 
2023 with good growth in all key markets. Availability of larger sizes 
improved during the year which aligned with strong demand in the 
foodservice segment.

In 2024, the contract share varied between the different business 
units. The Group's overall contract share was 27%, the same level 
as in 2023. The contract share for Norwegian origin was 23%.
The overall share of the volumes sold as superior quality was 87% 
in 2024, slightly down from 88% in 2023 and below the group 
target of at least 92%. Superior share was negatively affected by 
quality downgrading in Norway. This was the result of an unusually 
cold winter combined with a less efficacious vaccine for winter 
sores in recent years, compounded by the largest prevalence of 
string jellyfish for 20 years. On a positive note, biology in Norway in 
the 2024/2025 winter season has improved significantly following 
an improved vaccine for winter sores, operational improvements, 
less prevalence of string jellyfish as well as higher temperatures.
Segment Reporting 
The following is a presentation of our operating performance by 
business segment, using Operational EBIT per kg of fish harvested 
as a key measure of performance. The table below shows 
Operational EBIT for each of our operating segments for the years 
ended December 31, 2024 and 2023:
Feed
Operational EBITDA for our Feed segment of EUR 62.2 million 
was record-high and up from EUR 52.1 million in 2023 on good 
volumes and strong operational performance. Operational EBIT in 
2024 ended at EUR 46.8 million, up from the previous year (EUR 
35.5 million). Feed raw material costs have improved for most input 
factors, including marine ingredients, compared with 2023. The 
two most recent anchovy wild catch seasons in Peru in 2024 were 
strong with regards to volumes and yield, and this has contributed 
to a favourable raw material price development. Operational EBITDA 
margin was 5.5%, up from 4.9 % in 2023. 
Mowi Feed's core assets include a 460,000 tonne feed mill in 
Norway and a 240,000 tonne feed mill in Scotland. The two top 
modern mills have a combined capacity of 700,000 tonnes including 
an ongoing 60,000 tonnes capacity expansion expected to be 
fully operational in Q2 2026. In 2024, Mowi Feed sold 584 586 
tonnes, up from 523 167 tonnes in 2023 driven by good growth in 
our farming operations, and supplied 96% of the feed requirements 
of Mowi’s European salmon farming operations in 2024 (95% in 
2023). In March 2025, Mowi initiated a strategic review of the Feed 
division. The review will assess all available options, including a sale. 
The background for the strategic review is that Mowi has grown 
significantly in Farming in just a few years, and is approaching 600k 
Our Markets
Geographic market presence
Our main source of revenues is sale of Atlantic salmon. Europe is 
by far the largest market for our salmon, representing approximately 
70% of our total revenues in 2024 (71% in 2023). Mowi experienced 
good sales growth in most European countries. The UK, France and 
Germany continue to be very important markets. 
Compared with 2023, the relative share of sales to the American 
market increased slightly related to increase of harvest volumes in 
Canada and Chile. The relative share of sales to the Asian market in 
2024 was relatively stable compared with 2023.
Sales by product
The share of sales related to salmon products increased slightly 
compared with the previous year, at 94.7% and 94.1% of our 
revenues for the years ended December 31, 2024 and 2023 
respectively. Fresh whole salmon (i.e. primary processed salmon) 
represented 50.7% of our total revenues in 2024, relatively stable 
from 50.2% in 2023. In the same periods, elaborated salmon, 
including smoked/marinated, MAP, sushi and other prepared and 
value-added products accounted for 49.3% and 49.8% of our 
revenues respectively. 
For the market in general, the foodservice segment represents 
approx. 40%, while the retail segment represents approx. 60%.
Mowi has an aim of further increasing our capacity to produce 
elaborated and value-added products, which generally command 
more stable consumer prices. In line with this strategy, we have 
opened new value-added plants in several countries in recent 
years, and we have also expanded several of our existing plants. 
Consequently, we have good coverage of the main markets in 
Europe, the US and Asia.
Price achievement
As described in the previous section, market prices were somewhat 
down in 2024 from a high level in 2023. With regards to price 
achievement relative to the reference price, this was somewhat 
reduced in Norway driven by quality downgrading in the first half 
of the year. This effect was offset by improved price achievement 
in Scotland and other regions. Consequently, Mowi achieved a 
combined global price 2% above the weighted reference price in 
2024, same as in 2023. Relative to the reference price, contract 
sales including contribution from Consumer Products made a 
positive contribution also in 2024.

Farming
Farming’s Operational EBIT totalled EUR 443.8 million in the year 
ended December 31, 2024, compared with EUR 682.4 million in 
the year ended December 31, 2023. The reduction from the 2023 
Operational EBIT was mainly driven by lower achieved prices and 
realisation of higher cost. These effects were partly offset by higher 
volumes. Although realised P&L cost increased, cash cost to stock 
was reduced during 2024, and cost at stock per year end was EUR 
0.13 per kg LWT lower than the year before, driven by feed price 
decreases. This is expected to contribute to lower realised P&L cost 
in 2025. Mowi Farming continued to be the best or second best 
cost performer vs. peers in the various farming regions. Volumes 
were all-time high at 501 530 tonnes up from 474 664 in 2023, an 
increase of 5.7% y-o-y. Stocking of postsmolt to sea was all-time high 
in 2024 and volumes are expected to increase by another 5.7% to 
530k GWT in 2025, excluding Nova Sea. For details of our farming 
entities' operational performance, please see the comments under 
Operational performance by country of origin.
Sales and Marketing
Our Sales & Marketing operations consist of the reporting segments 
Markets (trading-related activities) and Consumer Products (valueadded operations). 
Markets
Markets’ Operational EBIT for the year came to EUR 206.5 million, 
compared with EUR 170.1 million in 2023. Revenue increased driven 
by higher volumes. The earnings effect of approx. EUR 29 million 
of upgrading downgraded salmon in Norway is included in the 
Markets segment and was higher than normal in 2024 due to the 
challenging winter sore situation. 
Consumer Products
Mowi Consumer Products is geographically organised, but 
constitutes one reporting segment. Consumer Products' Operational 
EBIT for the year ended December 31, 2024 came to a EUR 145.8 
million, slightly down from EUR 151.7 million in 2023. The negative 
effect of margin pressure in Europe was partly offset by higher 
volumes and continued first-class operational performance. The 
volume sold ended at 247 333 tonnes end-product weight, an 
increase from 232 169 tonnes in 2023.
Europe
Consumer Products Europe benefited from strong operational 
performance and increased volumes. Revenue increased on higher 
volumes. Good efficiency in production, value chain optimisations 
and yield improvements contributed positively. However, margin 
pressure compared with 2023 had a negative influence on earnings. 
Retail development was good overall, while foodservice was 
relatively stable. 
Americas
Volumes and earnings in Consumer Products Americas were 
relatively stable in 2024 compared with 2023. Earnings in the Chilled 
segment were good, while the Fresh segment in the US experienced 
margin pressure due to a more sluggish market, especially in the first 
half of 2024. Compared with Europe, the US market is still somewhat 
behind on the recovery curve. However, we expect demand to work 
itself out in due course. The second half of the year saw positive 
developments in the fresh pre-packed category in the retail segment. 
Asia
Our Asian operations saw increased volume in 2024 compared with 
2023. Operational performance was strong in most units. Improved 
availability of larger sizes as the year progressed had a positive 
impact, and this aligned with positive demand developments in the 
foodservice segment.

by reduced prices, partly offset by all-time high volumes and

strong operational performance. Full cost per kg salmon increased 
somewhat from 2023 on realisation of previous feed inflation. Other 
cost items were relatively stable y-o-y. Operational EBIT per kg was 
EUR 2.03 compared with EUR 2.82 in 2023. Our EBIT for salmon 
of Norwegian origin was EUR 685.3 million for the year ended 
December 31, 2024 compared with EUR 853.4 million in 2023. EBIT 
per kg was EUR 2.26 in 2024 compared with EUR 2.90 in 2023.
Price and volume developments
Harvest volumes of 303 501 tonnes in 2024 were the highest 
ever, and volumes are set to further increase to 315k GWT in 2025 
excluding Nova Sea. Volumes in 2029 including Nova Sea are 
expected to exceed 400k GWT.
The reference price for Atlantic salmon of Norwegian origin in 2024 
was reduced from record-high levels in 2023. Furthermore, price 
achievement was negatively impacted by quality downgrading 
in the first half. Since 2020, the winter sore vaccine has become 
less efficacious. This, combined with an unusually cold winter and 
the largest prevalence of string jellyfish for 20 years, negatively 
impacted superior share and prices. A new winter sore vaccine, 
helped by operational improvements, less string jellyfish and higher 
temperatures, have led to significantly improved biology in the 
2024/2025 winter season. 
Our price achievement for the year ended December 31, 2024 was 
3% below the reference price, compared with price achievement 
at the reference price level in 2023, driven by lower superior share 
of 83% vs. 86% in 2023. Contribution from contracts, including 
Consumer Products, was positive in 2024, same as in 2023. The 
contract share was 23% in 2024, compared with 25% in 2023. 
Costs and operations
Performance in Mowi Norway was strong in 2024 with all-time high 
seawater production and harvest volumes, high license utilisation 
and increased smolt stocking. Biological KPIs were improved, 
including net production and feed conversion ratio. Performance 
in Region West and Region South was particularly positive, while 
financial and biological performance in Region Mid was at a lower 
level than the other three regions. 
Region West had another strong year with strong biological KPIs and 
financial results, all-time high volumes and the highest margin of the 
four regions in Norway. Region South also had record-high volumes, 
and the region saw improvements in biological performance vs. 
2023 and a margin at the same level as Region North. Region 
North was impacted by somewhat lower volumes impacted by a PD 
incident towards the end of 2023, and experienced more pressure 
than usual from environmental conditions in 2024. Region Mid had 
another challenging year and the turnaround process is ongoing. 
Environmental conditions and low volumes negatively impacted full 
year results for this region.
Full cost per kg for salmon of Norwegian origin harvested in 2024 
increased slightly compared with 2023, as lower feed cost was 
offset by inflationary pressure on other items. Sea lice mitigation 
and treatment costs were relatively stable compared with 2023, 
and development of non-medicinal tools and methods continued 
in collaboration with Mowi's Global R&D and Technical department. 
Incident-based mortality costs totalled EUR 49.0 million in 2024, 
stable from EUR 48.9 million in 2023, mainly caused by gill issues 
and knock-on effects from lice treatments, in addition to winter sore 
issues.

Region South
For Region South, 2024 was another strong year with record-high 
volumes, good improvements in biological KPIs such as mortality 
and feed conversion ratio, and relatively good cost performance. 
Operational EBIT amounted to EUR 137.1 million in 2024 compared 
with EUR 221.2 million in 2023. The decrease was mainly due 
to lower prices and higher realised cost on the back of previous 
inflationary pressure, partly offset by dilution effect from higher 
harvest volume and lower realised feed cost. Operational EBIT 
per kg harvested was EUR 2.01, i.e. the second highest in our 
Norwegian operations in 2024, compared with EUR 3.33 in 2023. 
The volume harvested was all-time high 68 282 tonnes gutted 
weight, compared with 66 375 tonnes in 2023. Volumes were 
positively affected by strong seawater production and improved 
survival rate. 
Region West
Region West had yet another record year in 2024, and was our best 
performing region in Norway in 2024. Operational EBIT amounted 
to EUR 202.8 million in 2024 compared with EUR 226.8 million 
in 2023. The decrease was mainly due to lower achieved prices, 
partly offset by lower cost and higher harvest volumes. Feed cost 
were reduced by 4%, while other cost items were relatively stable. 
Harvest volumes ended at record-high 84 479 tonnes gutted weight 
compared with 81 937 tonnes in 2023 on overall good biological 
performance. Operational EBIT per kg harvested was EUR 2.40 vs. 
EUR 2.77 in 2023. 
Region Mid
Operational EBIT amounted to EUR 88.5 million in 2024 compared 
with EUR 72.2 million in 2023. Over time, performance in Mowi 
Region Mid has not been satisfactory compared with peers and 
other regions, and a turnaround process is ongoing. Harvest volume 
increased from 2023 on good production and reduced mortality in 
the first half of the year. Average harvest weight and superior share 
also improved from 2023. Cost improved from a high base in 2023 
driven by positive developments in the first half of 2024 and scale 
effects from higher volumes. In the second half of 2024 the region 
faced more troublesome biological challenges with string jellyfish 
and increased lice pressure. Volumes harvested increased to 56 
127 tonnes gutted weight from 47 065 tonnes in 2023 as a result 
of the above-mentioned improved production and biology in the 
first half of 2024. Operational EBIT per kg harvested was EUR 1.58, 
compared with EUR 1.53 in 2023. 
Region North
Operational EBIT in Region North amounted to EUR 188.0 million 
in 2024 compared with the record-high EUR 311.3 million in 2023. 
Harvest volumes were 94 551 tonnes gutted weight, down from 99 
124 tonnes in 2023 driven by enforced culling of small PD-positive 
fish at two sites towards the end of 2023. Region North also had 
more pressure than usual from environmental conditions in 2024, 
with winter sores and an unusually cold winter in the first half, 
exacerbated by string jellyfish, and record-high sea temperatures 
and high lice pressure in the autumn. Achieved prices were also 
reduced from 2023. The Operational EBIT margin was reduced to 
EUR 1.99 from EUR 3.14 in 2023. 
1) We measure our harvest volume in terms of tonnes of gutted weight of salmon. Harvest volume of salmon is a key measure of our success and is the 
volume-related driver of our profit. In the absence of trading, it corresponds to the volume of salmon available for sale.
2) The average price achievement measures the prices that we are able to achieve on our products compared with a salmon price index. Price achievement 
is measured against NASDAQ for salmon of Norwegian, Scottish and Faroese origin and Urner Barry for salmon of North American and Chilean origin. The 
market reference prices are spot prices for superior quality salmon, while our achieved price is a blend of spot and contract price for all qualities. Average 
price achievement measures our ability to sell our products at above market rates and is thus important for understanding our performance. In situations 
where contract prices deviate from spot prices, or the quality of our sold fish is low, our achieved price will deviate from the reference price.
3) The contract coverage measure represents the percentage of our products that was sold pursuant to contracts. A contract is for this purpose defined as a 
commitment to sell our salmon at a fixed price for a period of three months or longer. We have a sales contract policy aimed at limiting our exposure to short 
and medium-term fluctuations in salmon prices.
4) The superior share of salmon is the percentage graded as being of superior quality, divided by the total volume of harvested salmon. If salmon for some 
reason, e.g., pale colour or scale loss, cannot be classified as a superior product, it is downgraded and sold as production or ordinary grade product at a 
lower price.
5) Feed cost per kg harvested is calculated by dividing our total cost of fish feed for harvested fish by tonnes of gutted weight of salmon harvested.
6) Total cost per kg harvested is calculated by dividing our total cost for harvested fish by tonnes of gutted weight of salmon harvested.

Salmon of Scottish origin
Operational EBIT
Operational EBIT for salmon of Scottish origin was EUR 110.6 
million for the year ended December 31, 2024 compared with 
EUR 76.5 million in 2023. Biology was improved in 2024 with 
lower seawater temperatures and less issues with algae and 
jellyfish compared with 2023. Prices, cost and volumes were 
improved in 2024. 
Operational EBIT per kg was EUR 1.68 in 2024 compared with 
EUR 1.39 in 2023. Our EBIT for salmon of Scottish origin was EUR 
105.9 million for the year ended December 31, 2024 compared 
with EUR 76.0 million in 2023. EBIT per kg was EUR 1.60 in 2024 
compared with EUR 1.38 in 2023.
Price and volume developments
Achieved prices improved slightly in 2024. Our price 
achievement for salmon of Scottish origin for the year ended 
December 31, 2024 was 25% above the reference price, 
compared with 15% above in 2023. Contribution from contracts, 
including contribution from Consumer Products, was positive 
relative to the reference price in 2024 as they were in 2023. The 
contract share was 57% in 2024 compared with 56% in 2023. 
The superior share was 94% in 2024, stable from 94% also in 
2023. At 65 977 tonnes gutted weight, harvested volume in the 
year ended December 31, 2024 increased from 54 950 tonnes 
in 2023 on the back of increased full-year production and an 
improved biological situation. 
Costs and operations
Full cost per kg for salmon of Scottish origin harvested in 2024 
decreased compared with 2023 mainly as a result of decreased 
mortality cost on the back of improved biology and scale effects 
from higher harvest volumes, partly offset by general inflationary 
pressure. EUR 13.7 million was recognised as incident-based 
mortality in 2024, a significant reduction from EUR 24.4 million in 
2023.
The more challenging environmental conditions over the last years 
have called for more robust salmon and a shorter production cycle 
in sea in order to, amongst other things, avoid a second summer 
and autumn in sea. With this in mind, Mowi acquired the Dawnfresh 
bankruptcy estate's Loch Etive trout sites in 2023. Loch Etive is 
particularly suitable for postsmolt farming due to its brackish water. 
This will give us a total annual postsmolt production in Scotland of 7 
million smolt, equivalent to a coverage of 30%. Consequently, Mowi 
Scotland's postsmolt project has several benefits compared with 
a land-based facility, including lower capital expenditure, shorter 
realisation time and lower running production cost. In 2024 the first 
postsmolt produced in Loch Etive was transferred to ordinary sea 
sites, with harvesting commencing in 2025. 
Another important part of Mowi Scotland's biological turnaround 
plan is to become self-sufficient for eggs. Construction of the new 
broodstock facility at Ardessie in Northern Scotland is ongoing and 
is expected to be completed in 2025. When complete, it will provide 
a secure supply for 100% of Mowi Scotland's egg requirements. 
Salmon of Chilean origin
Operational EBIT
Our Operational EBIT for salmon of Chilean origin was EUR 57.5 
million for the year ended December 31, 2024 compared with EUR 
60.5 million in 2023. The overall biological situation as well as the 
cost level for Mowi Chile was good. Harvest volumes increased to 
all-time high levels and exceeded 70k tonnes for the first time since 
2008. However, market conditions for salmon of Chilean origin 
were difficult also in 2024 on the back of a more challenging US 
market. Operational EBIT per kg was EUR 0.79 in 2024 compared 
with EUR 0.87 in 2023. Our EBIT for salmon of Chilean origin was 
EUR 35.8 million in the year ended December 31, 2024 compared 
with EUR 37.1 million in 2023. EBIT per kg was EUR 0.49 in 2024 
compared with EUR 0.54 in 2023. 
Price and volume developments
Market prices for salmon of Chilean origin increased by 3.4% in 
2024 compared with 2023. Although demand was still somewhat 
lacklustre in 2024, the Chilean market regained some of the gap 
vs. Europe, with reference to the two-way division of the market 
since Q2 2023. Price achievement was 6% above the reference 
price in 2024, compared with 3% above the reference price in 
2023. Contracts had a positive effect on price achievement in both 
2024 and in 2023. The contract share was 29% in 2024 (30% in 
2023). 
The superior share for salmon of Chilean origin was 92% in 2024 
(91% in 2023), i.e. at the group target of 92%. Harvest volumes of 
72 694 tonnes gutted weight in 2024 were all-time high (69 199 
tonnes in 2023). 
Costs and operations
Overall biology was good in 2024, although with some issues 
driven by SRS which affected production and survival rates. On a 
positive note, harvest weights improved from 2023. SRS continues 
to be a challenge for Chilean salmon farming, and a new vaccine is 
being tested. 
Higher prevalence of lice has been managed by use of freshwater 
treatments from wellboats, with good results so far.
Cost increased slightly, but limited given the inflationary 
environment. Incident-based mortality in the amount of EUR 17.1 
million was recognised in 2024, which was an increase from EUR 
6.5 million in 2023.
Salmon of Canadian origin
Operational EBIT
Our Operational EBIT for salmon of Canadian origin was EUR 3.4 
million for the year ended December 31, 2024 compared with EUR 
18.9 million in 2023. Spot prices were reduced on more challenging 
market conditions, and this was the main driver behind the earnings 
decrease. Volumes from Canada West increased slightly from a low 
level in 2023 due to site mix. Volumes in Canada East was slightly 
down from 2023 on low opening biomass. Combined cost was 
stable; cost increased in Canada West due to an algae bloom in the 
summer, while cost decreased in Canada East.
Operational EBIT per kg was EUR 0.11 in 2024 compared with EUR 
0.66 in 2023. Our EBIT for salmon of Canadian origin was EUR -71.3 
million in the year ended December 31, 2024 compared with EUR 
-3.3 million in 2023. EBIT per kg was EUR -2.34 in 2024 compared 
with EUR -0.11 in 2023.
Price and volume developments
Market prices for salmon of Canadian origin decreased by 5.5% 
and 6.1% in West and East respectively versus 2023. Our price 
achievement in 2024 was 2% below the combined reference 
price, compared with 1% below in 2023. Price achievement was 
negatively impacted by quality downgrading. There were no 
contracts for salmon of Canadian origin in 2024, i.e. same as in 
2023. The superior share was 91% in 2024, compared with 91% in 
2023, slightly below the group target of 92%. 
The harvest volume in the year ended December 31, 2024 was 
30 426 tonnes gutted weight compared with 28 575 tonnes in 
2023. 
In Canada East, harvest volume decreased from 9 749 tonnes in 
2023 to 8 435 tonnes in 2024. In Canada West, harvest volumes 
were 21 991 tonnes in 2024 vs. 18 826 tonnes in 2023, positively 
impacted by uneven site mix. 
Costs and operations
Full cost per kg for salmon of Canadian origin harvested in the year 
ended December 31, 2024 was stable compared with 2023 on 
relatively stable volumes, but despite general inflationary pressure. 
Incident-based mortality of EUR 11.3 million was recognised in 2024 
in our Canadian operations (EUR 10.3 million in 2023) mainly related 
to algae and low oxygen levels in Canada West. 
In Canada East, volumes are expected to gradually increase over 
the coming years on increased smolt stocking while maintaining 
control over biology and cost. Following environmental and 
biological incidents in the aftermath of the acquisition of Canada 
East in 2018, biological performance in this region has now been 
good for several years. The cost level has also improved. Mowi has 
significant unutilised license capacity in this region.
In Canada West, Mowi has a 20k GWT level operation with 
uncertain future prospects following the authorities' decision in 
June 2024 to ban traditional marine salmon farming from mid-2029. 
Mowi has decided to initiate a strategic review of the Canada West 
business unit and will explore all available options before taking 
the appropriate action. The governmental decision in Canada West 
does not affect Canada East and Mowi’s strategy for that region.
Salmon of Irish origin
Operational EBIT
Our Operational EBIT for salmon of Irish origin was EUR 14.0 
million for the year ended December 31, 2024 compared with EUR 
1.2 million in 2023. Harvest volumes increased from a low level 
in 2023 due to previous biological issues. Cost was positively 
affected by increased harvest volumes. Prices were down from 
038 LEADING THE BLUE REVOLUTION STRATEGY BOARD STATEMENTS FINANCIAL STATEMENTS ANALYTICAL APPENDICES 039
high level in 2023, but prices for organic salmon were still good 
also in 2024. Operational EBIT per kg amounted to EUR 1.57 in 
2024 compared with EUR 0.27 in 2023. Our EBIT for salmon of Irish 
origin was EUR 13.2 million in the year ended December 31, 2024 
compared with EUR 3.1 million in the same period in 2023. EBIT per 
kg was EUR 1.48 in 2024 compared with EUR 0.69 in 2023.
Price and volume developments
Mowi Ireland mainly produces organic salmon and there is no 
reference price available for benchmarking. Compared with 2023, 
achieved prices were 6% lower for the year ended December 31, 
2024. As in previous years, earnings were positively impacted 
by sale of eggs. Our contract share was 60%, a decrease from 
87% in 2023. The superior share of salmon harvested was 92% 
in 2024 and 87% in 2023. The harvest volume in the year ended 
December 31, 2024 was 8 887 tonnes gutted weight compared with 
4 534 tonnes in 2023. 
Costs and operations
Full cost per kg for salmon of Irish origin harvested in the year 
ended December 31, 2024 decreased compared with 2023 driven 
by dilution effect from higher harvest volumes, partly offset by 
higher mortality cost. 2024 smolt have been vaccinated against 
SRS which is expected to have a positive impact in due course. 
Biological metrics improved in 2024, including seawater production, 
survival rate, feed conversion ratio, superior share and average 
harvest weights.
Salmon of Faroese origin
Operational EBIT
Our Operational EBIT for salmon of Faroese origin was EUR 22.7 
million for the year ended December 31, 2024 compared with EUR 
32.4 million in 2023. Mowi Faroes had another very good year in 
2024 with strong biology and stable prices, partly offset by slightly 
higher cost and lower volumes. Operational EBIT per kg was 
EUR 2.42 in 2024 compared with EUR 2.94 in 2023. Our EBIT for 
salmon of Faroese origin was EUR 25.2 million in the year ended 
December 31, 2024 compared with EUR 33.2 million in 2023. EBIT 
per kg was EUR 2.69 in 2024 compared with EUR 3.01 in 2023. 
Price and volume developments
Achieved prices in 2024 were 9% above the reference price level, 
compared with 2023 when the achieved prices were 4% above the 
reference price level. There were no contracts in Mowi Faroes in 
2024 or 2023. The harvest volume in the year ended December 31, 
2024 was 9 378 tonnes gutted weight compared with 11 027 tonnes 
in 2023. Harvest volumes fluctuate from year to year in our Faroese 
operations due to low number of sites. The strong biological 
performance was underlined by good average harvest weights and 
improved survival rate in 2024. The latter is at a very impressive 
level. As the biological situation was good, harvesting was kept low 
in order towards the end of 2024 to benefit from expected market 
improvements in 2025.
Costs and operations
In 2024, the cost level for salmon of Faroese origin was slightly 
increased compared with 2023 on inflationary pressure, but on a 
positive side realised feed cost was reduced compared to 2023. 
EUR 0.5 million was recognised as incident-based mortality in 2024, 
compared with none in 2023. 
Liquidity, Cash Flow and Borrowings 
Liquidity and capital resources
Our principal sources of liquidity are cash on hand, revenues 
generated from our operations, loans and other financings. Our 
principal needs for liquidity have been, and will likely continue to 
be, costs of raw materials, including fish feed, other working capital 
items and capital expenditures, to service our debt and to fund 
M&A activity and dividend payments. We believe that our liquidity is 
sufficient to cover our working capital needs in the ordinary course 
of business.
Our cash and cash equivalents as of December 31, 2024 was EUR 
290.2 million compared with EUR 302.8 million as of December 31, 
Salmon of Icelandic origin
Operational EBIT
Operational EBIT for salmon of Icelandic origin was EUR 14.7 million 
for the year ended December 31, 2024, compared with EUR 13.5 
million in 2023. Operational EBIT per kg was EUR 1.38 in 2024 (EUR 
1.14 in 2023). Our EBIT for salmon of Icelandic origin was EUR 13.7 
million in the year ended December 31, 2024, up from EUR -5.6 
million in 2023. EBIT per kg was EUR 1.29 in 2024 compared to EUR 
-0.47 per kg. in 2023. 
Price and volume developments
Prices for salmon of Icelandic origin had a positive development 
in 2024 compared with 2023. A new sales agreement with Mowi 
Sales & Marketing has been entered into, replacing Arctic Fish' old 
external agreement. The aim of the new agreement is to improve 
value realisation and market access. Price achievement in 2023 was 
negatively impacted by temporary logistics issues. There were no 
contracts on salmon of Icelandic origin in 2024. The harvest volume 
in the year ended December 31, 2024 was 10 667 tonnes gutted 
weight, a slight decrease from 11 878 tonnes in 2023. 
Costs and operations
Full operational cost increased in 2024 from 2023 on slightly lower 
harvest volume. The cost level in Iceland is still too high for Mowi 
and the rest of the industry, and streamlining of operations and cost 
reductions continue to be high priorities going forward. Biology 
improved from 2023 which had a positive effect on biological KPIs 
such as survival rate, feed conversion ratio, production and average 
harvest weight. 
Several measures have been taken the last years to improve 
operational and financial performance. Arctic Fish entered into 
a new feed contract with Mowi Feed from July 2023, and in the 
same month the new processing facility in Bolungarvík commenced 
operations. Consequently, Arctic Fish is no longer dependent 
on external harvesting capacity. This is expected to improve 
operational efficiency and the cost level going forward.
Our clear goal is to develop Arctic Fish into a streamlined and 
cost-effective operation. This includes improved lice strategy and 
treatment capacity which is a priority for the company, in addition 
to streamlining of the bureaucracy related to the Icelandic salmon 
industry.
2023. Cash and cash equivalents comprise cash and bank deposits, 
including restricted funds. Restricted funds are mainly related to 
employees’ income tax withholdings.
Our NIBD (excluding effects of IFRS 16) was EUR 1 867.1 million as of 
December 31, 2024, up from EUR 1 790.3 million as of December 31, 
2023, of which EUR 132.7 million in Arctic Fish. Per year-end, NIBD 
exceeded the long-term target of EUR 1 700 million, but Mowi will 
revert to a revised NIBD target following completion of the Nova 
Sea acquisition. 
Capital expenditures
Our capital expenditures primarily relate to investments in our 
operating facilities and equipment used in our operations. Net 
capital expenditures were approximately EUR 354.0 million for the 
year ended December 31, 2024, or EUR 290 million adjusted for 
acquisition of licenses in Norway. This was a decrease from EUR 
388.5 million for the year ended December 31, 2023. For 2024 
and 2023 respectively, EUR 203.6 million and EUR 221.8 million 
of the total net capital expenditure was attributable to our farming 
operations in Norway. The bulk of the capital expenditure in Norway 
was related to postsmolt projects and purchase of license capacity. 
Cash flows
Cash flow from operations
Cash flow from operations for the year ended December 31, 2024 
came to EUR 916.6 million, compared with EUR 992.2 million for 
2023. Adjusted for IFRS 16 effects, cash flow from operations 
was EUR 669.9 million in 2024 vs. EUR 782.1 million in 2023. The 
decrease was mainly related to lower operational earnings driven 
by lower prices. Working capital tie-up was lower in 2024 than in 
2023 due to lower feed prices and less inflationary pressure. Tax 
payments increased due to prepayments in Norway of EUR 81 
million which will reduce tax payments in 2025 accordingly. 
Cash flow from investments
Cash flow from investments for the year ended December 31, 
2024 came to EUR -332.1 million, compared with cash flow from 
investments of EUR -413.6 million in 2023. In both years, net capex 
was the main contributor, with EUR 290.0 million in 2024 vs. EUR 
362.2 million in 2023. The reduction was due to several large 
projects being completed, including postsmolt facilities in Norway 
and the new processing facility in Region Mid. Norway. 
In addition, acquisition of license capacity in Norway amounted to 
EUR 64.0 million in 2024 vs. EUR 26.3 million in the residual auction 
in 2023. 
Furthermore, other investments include a net cash inflow of EUR 
21.9 million in 2024 related to dividends from associates vs. a net 
cash outflow of EUR 25.3 million in 2023. The 2023 figure includes 
the acquisition of assets from the Dawnfresh bankruptcy estate in 
Scotland related to the postsmolt programme for Mowi Scotland. 
Cash flow from financing
Cash flow from financing for the year ended December 31, 2024 
came to EUR -598.3 million, compared with EUR -458.2 million for 
2023. This includes effects of proceeds from interest-bearing debt 
and down payments of leasing debt. Cash flow outflows related to 
dividends decreased from EUR 326.1 million in 2023 to 292.2 million 
in 2024 on lower earnings, while interest expenses increased from 
2023 to 2024. 
Borrowings
As of December 31, 2024 our main outstanding borrowings 
consisted of the EUR 2 000 million secured sustainability-linked 
facility maturing in 2026, a green unsecured bond of EUR 213 
million maturing in 2029, a green unsecured bond of EUR 85 
million maturing in 2032, a green unsecured bond of EUR 200 
million which matured in January 2025 and was repaid, as well as 
an unsecured Schuldschein loan of EUR 150 million maturing in 
2026. Arctic Fish has a separate financing. For further details of 
our borrowing facilities and bonds, please see Note 11 to the Group 
financial statement and for further details of how to analyse our 
performance, please see Part IV - Analytical Information.

Aquatic animal foods provide
Production of food from the ocean 
makes sense 
From the United Nations (FAO, UN Global Compact) to world-leading 
scientists there is an overall agreement that food from the ocean is a 
triple win: for people because it is healthy, for the planet because it 
is climate-friendly, and for the economy because it sustains local and 
global economies. 
Aquaculture has already surpassed capture fisheries in aquatic 
animal production and the latest FAO report on the State of World 
Fisheries and Aquaculture (SOFIA, 2024) clearly recognises the 
role of aquatic animal foods, including salmon, to reduce food and 
nutrition insecurity and tackle many forms of malnutrition, providing 
high-quality nutrients with a moderate energy contribution. 
The Blue Food Assessment, the High Level Panel for a Sustainable 
Ocean Economy and FAO's Blue Transformation roadmap, continue 
to provide a credible and transparent assessment of the potential for 
aquaculture as a sustainable ocean economy. Blue foods have lower 
environmental footprints than land-based foods. Farmed salmon, in 
particular, has lower GHG emissions , water use and land use per kg 
of edible weight when compared with chicken. Taking an industry 
average, farm-raised Norwegian salmon has an emissions intensity 
that is 20% that of beef (SINTEF, 2020). The carbon footprint of 
farm-raised salmon is 6.4 kg of carbon equivalent per kg of edible 
product, compared with 12.2 kg of carbon equivalent per edible kg of 
pork and 39.0 kg per edible kg of beef (SINTEF, 2020, 2022).
For the consumer, replacing pork and beef with fish would 
significantly reduce their personal carbon footprint. Not only is the 
carbon footprint of farm-raised salmon lower but its edible yield is 
higher (68%) as compared with chicken (46%), pork (52%) or lamb 
(38%). For Mowi, high edible yields combined with 100% re-use of 
by-products (i.e.offcuts and trimmings) means that nearly every single 
gram of salmon is used, thereby avoiding food waste.
Mowi's vision of Leading the Blue Revolution and our sustainability 
strategy are aimed at realising the potential of blue foods, ie making 
more healthy and sustainable food from the ocean available to an 
increasing world population. In 2024, we further implemented our 
sustainability strategy with the achievement of key milestones such 
as:
 update of our climate targets aligned with 1.5˚C
 development of our CSRD aligned climate transition plan
 update of our CDP Climate and Water report and our 
biodiversity framework (Farming in Harmony with Nature)
 inclusion of the aquaculture sector guidance in our TNFD report, 
and 
 significant progress towards reduction of our scope 1 and 2 
emissions as well our scope 3 (FLAG) emissions.
